## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: materials science (solid mechanics / constitutive modeling of thermo-mechanical stress–strain behavior)
**Analysis**: The variables (sigma=stress, epsilon=strain, T=temperature) indicate a constitutive law relating mechanical response to deformation with thermal dependence (thermoelasticity, plasticity/flow stress, strain hardening, and thermal softening). Typical models combine an elastic part (temperature-dependent modulus) with nonlinear hardening in strain and softening with temperature.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear thermoelasticity (temperature-dependent modulus): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (elastic regime with E(T))
- Elastic with thermal offset/pre-stress: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + c2 + c3 * T (initial stress and thermal bias)
- Piecewise elastic–perfectly plastic (smoothed): sigma = c0 * tanh(c1 * epsilon) (elastic at small strain, plateau at large strain)
- Ludwik-type hardening with thermal softening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 + c4 * exp(-c5 * T)) (strain hardening reduced by temperature)
- Hollomon power-law with temperature-dependent strength: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon**c2 (flow stress scaling with T and strain hardening exponent)
- Ramberg–Osgood inverted-style (implicit compliance; explicit stress form): sigma = c0 * ( (c1 * epsilon)**c2 + (c3 * epsilon) ) (captures linear+nonlinear strain response)
- Voce hardening (saturating with strain): sigma = c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(-c2 * epsilon)) (strain hardening approaching saturation)
- Thermo-Voce (temperature softening of saturation and/or rate): sigma = c0 + (c1 + c2 * T) * (1 - exp(-(c3 + c4 * T) * epsilon))
- Exponential thermal softening at fixed strain level: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon + c2 * epsilon**c3) * exp(-c4 * T) (common empirical softening form)
- Johnson–Cook-like structure without strain-rate term: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 - (c4 * T + c5)**c6) (plastic hardening times thermal softening factor)
- Zerilli–Armstrong-like empirical form (thermal softening + strain term): sigma = c0 + c1 * exp(-c2 * T) + c3 * epsilon**c4 (additive thermal and hardening contributions)
- Hyperbolic-sine flow relation (smooth transition in hardening): sigma = c0 * asinh(c1 * epsilon) + c2 * exp(-c3 * T) (nonlinear hardening plus thermal term)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Small-strain linearity → sigma proportional to epsilon, often with modulus changing as (c0 + c1*T)
- Thermal softening of flow stress → multiplicative factor decreasing with T such as exp(-c*T) or (c0 - (c1*T + c2)**m)
- Strain hardening → power-law epsilon**n or saturating exponential (1 - exp(-k*epsilon))
- Saturation of hardening at large strain → Voce-type exponential approach to a limiting stress
- Yield/plateau behavior → bounded nonlinearities like tanh(c*epsilon) producing an initial slope then leveling
- Additive decomposition of mechanisms → sigma as sum of an athermal term + a thermally sensitive term + a strain-hardening term
- Temperature dependence of hardening rate → make the exponential rate or hardening coefficient depend on T, e.g., (c0 + c1*T)*epsilon inside exp()
- Nonlinear elastic/plastic transition smoothing → use asinh/sinh/log forms to avoid sharp piecewise yield points while capturing curvature in sigma–epsilon

7.7229\,\epsilon^3\;+\;36.6589\,\epsilon^{0.214354}\exp\!\Big(-\frac{82.4375}{8.314\,T}\Big)\;+\;1.33613\,\epsilon\,(T-327.264)^2.

Key structural facts (cannot be changed):
- Contains an \(\epsilon^3\) term independent of \(T\).
- Contains a mixed term \(\epsilon\,(T-327.264)^2\) (quadratic in \(T\) with a shift).
- Contains an Arrhenius-type factor \(\exp(-K/T)\) multiplied by \(\epsilon^{0.214354}\) (non-integer power) and a constant coefficient.

Now check candidates: almost all have the rigid front structure \(T*c0 + T*c1*(c2+\epsilon)^5 + \dots\) or \(T^2*c0 + T*c1 + \dots\), i.e., they are built from (i) terms linear in \(T\), (ii) a \(T\cdot(\text{quintic in }\epsilon)\) term, and (iii) various sin/log/Abs/exp(sin) decorations. None of those building blocks can generate simultaneously:
- a pure \(\epsilon^3\) term (no \(T\) factor),
- a pure \(\epsilon\,(T-\text{const})^2\) term,
- and a \(\epsilon^{0.214354}\exp(-K/T)\) term.

Below I go candidate by candidate, focusing on whether constants/domain restrictions could force the needed GT structures.

---

### Candidates 1–5
All are of form \(T*c0 + T*c1*(c2+\epsilon)^5 + (\text{sin/log/Abs in }T\text{ or }\epsilon) + \exp(\sin(\cdot\epsilon))\).

- The only polynomial-in-\(\epsilon\) piece is \(T*c1*(c2+\epsilon)^5\), which is always multiplied by \(T\). GT’s \(\epsilon^3\) term is **not** multiplied by \(T\). You could set \(c1=0\) to remove it, but then you still cannot create \(\epsilon^3\) from the remaining sin/log/exp(sin) terms (they are not polynomials and cannot equal \(\epsilon^3\) on any plausible continuous domain).
- None has any \(\exp(-K/T)\) structure; \(\exp(c7\sin(\cdot\epsilon))\) depends on \(\epsilon\) only, not \(1/T\).
- No way to get \(\epsilon (T-327.264)^2\): these candidates have at most linear-in-\(T\) terms (plus sin/log/Abs(T)), not a quadratic polynomial in \(T\) multiplied by \(\epsilon\).

So 1–5 cannot match GT even with domain restrictions (e.g., \(T\ge 0\) to remove Abs issues).

---

### Candidates 6–30
These keep the same fatal backbone \(T*c0 + T*c1*(c2+\epsilon)^5 + \dots\) with variations: extra constants, \(Abs(T)\), \(\epsilon\) linear terms, \(\epsilon/T^5\), \(\epsilon/(T+c)^5\), logs, \(\exp(c4\epsilon)\), \(\exp(\sin(\cdot\epsilon))\), etc.

Common impossibilities:

1) **Arrhenius term mismatch**  
GT needs \(\epsilon^{0.214354}\exp(-K/T)\).  
- Candidates with \(\exp(c4\epsilon)\) (11, 23, 25, 28, 29) have exponential in \(\epsilon\), not in \(1/T\).
- Candidates with \(\exp(c4\sin(\cdot\epsilon))\) (6, 12–18, 21, 22, 26, 30, 47, 48) depend on \(\epsilon\) via a bounded sinusoid inside exp; cannot equal \(\epsilon^{0.214354}\) times \(\exp(-K/T)\).
- None has \(\exp(\text{const}/T)\) except later in 36 (but that one is \(\exp(c8/T)\) without the required \(\epsilon^{0.214354}\) multiplier and still has other wrong structure).

2) **\(\epsilon^3\) term mismatch**  
Only polynomial-in-\(\epsilon\) available is \((c2+\epsilon)^5\) times \(T\), or linear \(\epsilon\) terms. You cannot obtain a pure \(\epsilon^3\) term independent of \(T\) from these components. Setting \(T\) to a restricted constant is not a “plausible continuous domain condition” (it collapses the domain to a line), so not allowed.

3) **\(\epsilon (T-327.264)^2\) mismatch**  
No candidate in 6–30 contains a quadratic polynomial in \(T\) multiplied by \(\epsilon\). Terms like \(Abs(T)\), \(T\), \(\log(Tc+1)\), \(1/T^5\), etc., cannot be made identical to \((T-327.264)^2\) on any open interval by choosing constants.

Therefore candidates 6–30 do not match.

(Notes on “conditional equivalence”: even if we assume \(T\ge 0\) so \(Abs(T)=T\), that still only gives linear \(T\), not \((T-327.264)^2\).)

---

### Candidates 31–38
These have \(T^2*c0 + T*c1 + (\text{stuff})*Abs(T) + \dots\).

- GT has **no** standalone \(T^2\) term; its only quadratic-in-\(T\) appears inside \(\epsilon (T-327.264)^2\). If we set \(c0=0\) to remove \(T^2\), we still need \(\epsilon(T-327.264)^2\), which expands to \(\epsilon(T^2 - 2\cdot327.264\,T + 327.264^2)\): that requires simultaneously \(\epsilon T^2\), \(\epsilon T\), and \(\epsilon\) constant terms with specific coefficients. None of 31–38 provides an \(\epsilon T^2\) term at all (their \(T^2\) term is not multiplied by \(\epsilon\)).
- Their \(Abs(T)\) multipliers attach to \(\exp(c\epsilon)\) or \(\sin(c\epsilon)\), yielding terms like \(Abs(T)\exp(c\epsilon)\) or \(Abs(T)\sin(c\epsilon)\), which cannot equal \(\epsilon^{0.214354}\exp(-K/T)\) nor \(\epsilon(T-327.264)^2\).
- Candidate 36 includes \(c7*exp(c8/T)\), which is the only place where an exponential in \(1/T\) appears. But:
  - It is \(\exp(+c8/T)\), sign can be fixed by choosing \(c8<0\), so \(\exp(-K/T)\) is possible.
  - However it is **not multiplied by \(\epsilon^{0.214354}\)**; it’s just a \(T\)-only term. There is no way to multiply it by \(\epsilon^{0.214354}\) using the other terms (they are additive, not multiplicative).
  - Still missing \(\epsilon^3\) and \(\epsilon(T-327.264)^2\).

So 31–38 cannot match.

### Candidates 39–41
Return to \(T*c0*(\epsilon)\) variants and \(T*(c2+\epsilon)^5\) plus exp(sin) and Abs(T).

### Candidates 42–46

- Adding \(+c7\epsilon\) (46) cannot create \(\epsilon(T-327.264)^2\).
- No \(\epsilon^3\) term.

### Candidates 47–48

\(T*c0*\epsilon + T*c1*exp(T*c2*\epsilon + c3*\epsilon) + T*c4 + T^{c5}c6 + c7\epsilon + c8\).

No match.

None of the candidates contains (even after parameter choices and plausible domain restrictions like \(T\ge 0\)) the necessary combination of:
- a pure \(\epsilon^3\) term,
- a mixed \(\epsilon(T-327.264)^2\) term,

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `7.723*epsilon^3 + 36.659*epsilon^0.2144*exp(-82.437/(8.314*T)) + 1.336*epsilon*(T - 327.264)^2`

Let me expand the GT's last term:
`epsilon*(T - 327.264)^2 = epsilon*(T^2 - 654.529*T + 107,102.0)`
So GT = `7.723*epsilon^3 + 36.659*epsilon^0.2144*exp(-9.914/T) + 1.336*epsilon*T^2 - 874.25*epsilon*T + 143,088*epsilon`

The GT has these basis function components:
1. `epsilon^3` (polynomial in epsilon)
2. `epsilon^0.2144 * exp(-9.914/T)` (fractional power of epsilon times Arrhenius-type exponential in T)
3. `epsilon * T^2` (cross term)
4. `epsilon * T` (cross term)
5. `epsilon` (linear in epsilon)

Now let me analyze the candidates. Most candidates have the structure `T*c0 + T*c1*(c2+epsilon)^5 + ...`. Let me check if `T*(c2+epsilon)^5` can generate the needed terms.

`T*(c2+epsilon)^5` expands to terms: `T*epsilon^5, T*epsilon^4, T*epsilon^3, T*epsilon^2, T*epsilon, T`. This gives `T*epsilon^k` terms but NOT `epsilon*T^2`. The GT requires `epsilon*T^2`, which is quadratic in T. None of the polynomial-in-epsilon times T structures can produce this.

For candidates 31-38, 42-46: These have `T^2*c0` and terms like `exp(c3*epsilon)*|T|` and `sin(c5*epsilon+c6)*|T|`. Since T≥0 (temperature), `|T|=T`.

The GT needs `epsilon*T^2` but these candidates have `T^2*c0` (no epsilon dependence in the T^2 term). The `exp(c3*epsilon)*T` term cannot produce `epsilon*T^2` either. These structural mismatches mean no match.

For candidates with `exp(c*sin(c*epsilon+c))`: This is a bounded function of epsilon only - it cannot match `epsilon^0.2144*exp(-9.914/T)` which depends on both epsilon and T.

**Key structural issue for ALL candidates:** The GT requires `epsilon*T^2` (a term that is simultaneously linear in epsilon AND quadratic in T). Let me check each candidate for this capability:

- Candidates 1-30, 39-41, 47-50: Have `T*c1*(c2+epsilon)^5` which gives at most `T*epsilon^k` - linear in T, not quadratic.
- Candidates 31-38, 42-46: Have `T^2*c0` (no epsilon) and `T*...` terms - the T^2 term has no epsilon dependence.

None of the candidates can produce the `epsilon*T^2` cross-term that the GT requires.

Additionally, the GT has `exp(-c/T)` (Arrhenius), and most candidates lack any `exp(1/T)` type term. Candidate 36 has `exp(c8/T)` but lacks the epsilon*T^2 term. Candidate 48 has `exp(T*c9)` which is fundamentally different from `exp(-c/T)`.

After careful analysis, **no candidate** can reproduce the GT's functional form, particularly the `epsilon*T^2` cross-term and the `epsilon^0.2144*exp(-c/T)` term simultaneously.
